  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0f506695-11cb-4c2d-9343-54b18ee965f4'

<span id="freeTextContainer15211354721939836022"><i>End of Days</i> is the explosive conclusion to Susan Ee’s bestselling Penryn & the End of Days trilogy.   <span id="freeText15211354721939836022" style="display:none"><i>End of Days</i> is the explosive conclusion to Susan Ee’s bestselling Penryn &amp; the End of Days trilogy. After a daring escape from the angels, Penryn and Raffe are on the run. They’re both desperate to find a doctor who can reverse the twisted changes inflicted by the angels on Raffe and Penryn’s sister. As they set off in search of answers, a startling revelation about Raffe’s past unleashes dark forces that threaten them all.<br /><br />When the angels release an apocalyptic nightmare onto humans, both sides are set on a path toward war. As unlikely alliances form and strategies shift, who will emerge victorious? Forced to pick sides in the fight for control of the earthly realm, Raffe and Penryn must choose: Their own kind, or each other?</span>
  <a data-text-id="15211354721939836022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_899603778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/899603778" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/899603778?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444778557" href="/book/show/13638020-end-of-days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=apocalypse-rah">apocalypse-rah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=ya-pnr-maddness">ya-pnr-maddness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer899603778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11468908831946806064">This is a review for the much awaited conclusion of Penryn and The End of Days trilogy. I'm still waiting for this much awaited conclusion because I refuse to believe what I just read was it.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430904265ra/14777140.gif' alt='Nope' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It's not that End of Days was necessarily bad or poorly written. No, it's not that. The writing is consistent with her previous novels and the novel itself was reasonably satisfactory. But I didn't want satisfactory for the end of Penryn and Raffe's journey.<br/><br/>This was supposed to be epic. Earth shattering. The</span>
  <span id="freeText11468908831946806064" style="display:none">This is a review for the much awaited conclusion of Penryn and The End of Days trilogy. I'm still waiting for this much awaited conclusion because I refuse to believe what I just read was it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430904265ra/14777140.gif" alt="Nope" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's not that End of Days was necessarily bad or poorly written. No, it's not that. The writing is consistent with her previous novels and the novel itself was reasonably satisfactory. But I didn't want satisfactory for the end of Penryn and Raffe's journey.<br><br>This was supposed to be epic. Earth shattering. The emotions were supposed to be soaring out of control on a unicorn with no sense of direction except for up! This was supposed to be a roller coaster ride of emotions that doesn't stop until everyone on it has puked on each other's faces.<br><br>There was more emotion, sexual tension and drama in Angelfalls pinky finger than in End of Days' whole body. Where did that raw emotional connection go? What happened with these characters that they are just so blasé about each other and that I am, in turn, blasé about them?<br><br>God, by the end of the book I was just like:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430904265ra/14777141.gif" alt="yawn" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I'm not trying to be mean about this. I know it's hard to really knock it out of the park, but that's what this series deserved. It was owed so much more than this. I'm angriest because I know that Ee has it in her to wring truly powerful moments of raw emotion from her characters and readers. I felt it when Penryn was paralysed in Angelfall. I felt it when Raffe first realised Penryn was alive again in World After.<br><br>Yet I honestly can't think of a single moment of End of Days that sticks out to me as emotive or heartfelt. No single moment where my heart ached for the characters or the situation. Not a single Eeism, which I define as a condition when you want to marry a book because it gave you so many feels.<br><br>This isn't the review I wanted to be writing for End of Days. I kind of wish, now, that I had never read it and could keep going on imagining something more epic for these Starcrossed Lovers. Something that would do the story justice as a final book.<br><br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="11468908831946806064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_448943422" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/448943422" />
    <a title="Ails" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12873266-ails"><img alt="Ails" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351577137p2/12873266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/448943422?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ails" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ails" href="/user/show/12873266-ails">Ails</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=badass-female">badass-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=book-boyfriend">book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=swoon-worthy">swoon-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=most-anticipated-2015">most-anticipated-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer448943422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12471237130787282772"><b>5 STARS</b><br/><br/>UPDATE: FULL REVIEW (WARNING: MINOR SPOILERS)<br/><br/><i>(Join our End of Days discussion here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/2229350-end-of-days-warning-spoilers'>https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a>)</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Someone has sprayed graffiti on the ceiling. A crude knight stands alone with his sword drawn against a fire-breathing dragon that is ten times his size. The dragon's tail disappears into darkness where the window light fades deep into the store. Beside the knight are the words “Where Have All the Heroes Gone?”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431266819i/14815998._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>It looks to me like the artist thou</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12471237130787282772" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b><br><br>UPDATE: FULL REVIEW (WARNING: MINOR SPOILERS)<br><br><i>(Join our End of Days discussion here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/2229350-end-of-days-warning-spoilers">https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a>)</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Someone has sprayed graffiti on the ceiling. A crude knight stands alone with his sword drawn against a fire-breathing dragon that is ten times his size. The dragon's tail disappears into darkness where the window light fades deep into the store. Beside the knight are the words “Where Have All the Heroes Gone?”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431266819i/14815998._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>It looks to me like the artist thought the knight didn’t stand a chance against the dragon.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I know just how he feels."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>End of Days</b> is a very fitting title for this book not only because it's the end of this wonderful and outstanding series, but also because it's the end of my 'can't wait for the next book' and 'I'm dying in anticipation' days. It's been three months since I read it, and I still can't wrap my head around the fact that it's over.<br><br>To sum this book up in 10 words, "It is everything I wanted it to be—and more."<br><br>It begins right where World After left off—Raffe with Penryn in his arms, flying, and Paige sitting on Beliel's body which is being carried by scorpion-tailed locusts. Please take note that if you're currently reading this book, Penryn and Raffe's reunion just happened the night before. Their first meeting in Angelfall happened roughly two weeks ago because Angelfall and World After covers about ten days of their journey <i>(you can reread the books to verify. Thanks to Katerina for helping me count!)</i> That's how <b>packed</b> and huge this series is. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Who’s going to do that?”<br>I think about that for a minute before answering.<br>“Heroes.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Penryn, while being unconsciously cute and adorable, has always been a self-reliant and strong female character but in this final installment, Susan Ee takes her badass quality to a whole new level. She's not just a brave human girl; she's a fighter. <u>She represents humanity. <b>A Daughter of Man.</b></u><br><br>Raffe, on the otherhand, has always been a fierce believer and follower of angelic rules but in this book, the battle between his responsibilities and his heart gets tougher. He's not just an archangel; he's a warrior. <u>He represents the angels. <b>An enemy soldier.</b></u><br><br>He can't be distracted by a Daughter of Man, but the fire can be tempting. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Just this once,” he says almost more to himself than to me. “Just one moment.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>The romance in this series has always been subtle yet powerful—a gaze, a heart-melting smile, a conscious decision to hold each other a bit longer than necessary; such simple gestures speak volumes and enough to make me go crazy. Imagine my shock—and utter delight, when the romance got more <i>intense</i> in this book. Remember that in their world, it's just last night when Raffe found out Penryn was alive. The way he treats Penryn in World After was just the start. *wink wink*<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So am I?” I whisper. “Your Daughter of Man?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I am madly inlove with Raffe and Penryn's relationship not only because of their intense chemistry, but also because of their great camaraderie. He's not just an angel to her, she's not just a human to him; they're partners. <u>They represent their own race, but they're loyal to each other. <b>A team.</b></u><br><br><u>ENDING</u><br><br>A lot of people have been asking me, "I've read mixed reviews about this book. Some readers are euphoric, some are unsatisfied. Is it a happy ever after?" First of all, I'd waited more than a year for this book and the last six months had been the hardest for me because it's the period of time where I religiously checked my email for any response from the publisher about my ARC. I was like, "I might receive my advance reader's copy any day now yay!" (I know, right? Desperate!) The anticipation was so <i>huge</i> that it eventually felt like the book needed to make up for it. If this book was any less than remarkable, I'd be very, very disappointed. I don't know why some readers are unsatisfied, I guess reading the first two books again and again plus theorising about the conclusion for two years helped me appreciate this book more.<br><br>Some of my questions were left unanswered, but I wasn't really expecting every loose thread to be tied up so I was rather impressed that this book had exceeded my expectations and gave me more than what I wanted: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the epic war, the Watchers, the adventure in the pit, and the well-developed romance. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I would've wanted the buildup of the war to be shorter and the last chapters to be longer, but overall it's a very epic finale.<br><br><u>HAPPY EVER AFTER</u><br><br>Now let me ask you, what's your idea of a HEA or happy ever after? If it's ribbons and wedding bells and sparkles, then no, Raffe and Penryn didn't get their HEA. Sacrifices had to be made. The future in this apocalyptic world was ever unclear. If you theorize enough about it, if you consider all other possible alternate endings, you will realize it's the best and perfect conclusion to this series. When I finished the book, I had this satisfied look on my face and I thought "Of course! That's exactly the HEA this series deserves."<br><br>All the books in this series have wings on the cover. It has always been about it—it's the reason Raffe teamed up with Penryn in Angelfall, it's the reason they fought for their lives in World After. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Before EOD, I'd been very against the idea of Raffe losing his wings again. But what happened was he lost it for Penryn and this time <i>it's a choice made by him</i> so it's very justified for me. Susan Ee wanted us to feel the gravity of Raffe's feelings for Penryn that even after everything they've been through to get his wings back, he's willing to lose it again and again if it means Penryn gets to live another day. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The wings have always played a crucial part in their lives since day one, and it makes so much sense that it will continue to play an important role until the last book. It had brought them together. <b>It will bring them together. </b><br><br>•••<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"And now there’s this. Knowing about the horrors that have happened and will happen but choosing to live anyway. Maybe there’s an art to being human."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>In a war between humans and angels, the former represents the knight; the latter represents the dragon. The humans—the healthy, the injured, the young and old—they know they'll most likely be massacred but they come to fight anyway. <b>Heroes.</b><br><br>Overall, <b>End of Days</b> is an epic and a very justified ending to Penryn's story. (Oh my God I can't believe that this time I'm saying goodbye to this series but..) <br><br>Goodbye, Penryn and Raffe. <br><br>Goodbye, Mom, Paige, Dee Dum, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The Watchers,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>and Kooky—I mean Pooky Bear.<br><br>Goodbye, the one of the best apocalyptic dystopian series I've ever read.<br><br>It's a new day in End of Days.<br><br><i>(P.S. I might edit this review after the release date.)</i><br><br><i>
  <b>UPDATE: 02/24/15</b>
</i><br><br><i>(Thanks to the publisher for my advance reader's copy! View my status updates here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/60431809">http://www.goodreads.com/user_status/...</a>)</i><br><br>YOU GUYS ARE IN FOR A TREAT!!<br><br>THE ONLY WAY I CAN ACCURATELY DESCRIBE MY EMOTIONS (WITHOUT SPOILING) IS WITH THIS:<br><br>ON THE FIRST PAGES I WAS LIKE<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384187572ra/6807751.gif" width="250" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND THEN<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424866553ra/13811801.gif" width="250" height="170" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND AFTER THAT<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384188055ra/6808052.gif" height="250" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>ALMOST HALFWAY THROUGH THE BOOK I WAS LIKE<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424868067ra/13812046.gif" width="250" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND THEN<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424867661ra/13811978.gif" width="250" height="130" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND THEN AFTER THAT<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424867661ra/13811977.gif" width="250" height="170" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>ENDING:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424868068ra/13812047.gif" width="250" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>YEP, MY LIPS ARE SEALED! <br><br>FULL REVIEW TO BE POSTED CLOSER TO THE RELEASE DATE.<br><br><br><i>

<span id="freeTextContainer14900921603618157175"><i>“This is the way the series ends:<br/>Not with a bang, but a whimper.”</i><br/><br/>― T.S. Emily<br/><br/>Though <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17849112.World_After__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___2_' title='World After (Penryn & the End of Days, #2) by Susan Ee' rel='nofollow noopener'>World After</a> wasn't bad, I think this series reached a glorious high at the end of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_' title='Angelfall (Penryn & the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angelfall</a> and never quite reached the same heights again. It's just speculation, but part of me wonders if the author had no idea where she wanted to take it after the first book. Especially given that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_' title='Angelfall (Penryn & the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angelfall</a> was self-published back at a time when that pretty much guaranteed no one would read it. Everyone was surprised when it be</span>
  <span id="freeText14900921603618157175" style="display:none"><i>“This is the way the series ends:<br />Not with a bang, but a whimper.”</i><br /><br />― T.S. Emily<br /><br />Though <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17849112.World_After__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___2_" title="World After (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #2) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">World After</a> wasn't bad, I think this series reached a glorious high at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a> and never quite reached the same heights again. It's just speculation, but part of me wonders if the author had no idea where she wanted to take it after the first book. Especially given that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a> was self-published back at a time when that pretty much guaranteed no one would read it. Everyone was surprised when it became a huge success and perhaps Ms Ee was most surprised of all(?)<br /><br />This book is just fine - not badly written, but I didn't feel a single emotion while reading it.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1427423001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16020230971978342322">I'm the type of person who loves blood, gore, and explosions. The more the better. Or so I thought.<br/><br/>Years ago, I watched this movie in theatres. <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1217613/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Battle: Los Angeles</a>. It was AWESOME at first. Explosions! Death! People being blown into bits. Boom! Boom! Pow! Every other minute something exploded. It was great.<br/><br/>For about half an hour.<br/><br/>And then I just got SO bored. Like when was this going to end? There was too much action that it bored the hell out of me. I lost all attachment and enjoyment in the mov</span>
  <span id="freeText16020230971978342322" style="display:none">I'm the type of person who loves blood, gore, and explosions. The more the better. Or so I thought.<br /><br />Years ago, I watched this movie in theatres. <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1217613/" rel="nofollow noopener">Battle: Los Angeles</a>. It was AWESOME at first. Explosions! Death! People being blown into bits. Boom! Boom! Pow! Every other minute something exploded. It was great.<br /><br />For about half an hour.<br /><br />And then I just got SO bored. Like when was this going to end? There was too much action that it bored the hell out of me. I lost all attachment and enjoyment in the movie, and in the end, I just sat there for the remainder of the film, falling asleep as things were getting blasted into pieces on the screen in front of me. I just had enough.<br /><br />I think that was what ended up happening to this book. I just got sick of it. There was nothing overtly wrong with it; the characters were fine. The romance wasn't too much. It was just...all the action finally got to me; it was more or less a repetition of the first couple of books in a different form, and <b>I wanted something more from this series that this book didn't deliver</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16020230971978342322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_772435874" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/772435874" />
    <a title="Serena (The Book Comedian)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12242598-serena-the-book-comedian"><img alt="Serena (The Book Comedian)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421807323p2/12242598.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/772435874?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Serena (The Book Comedian)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Serena (The Book Comedian)" href="/user/show/12242598-serena-the-book-comedian">Serena (The Book Comedian)</a>
      </span>

          marked it as will-give-it-a-2nd-shot-eventually


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444778557" href="/book/show/13638020-end-of-days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12242598-serena-the-book-comedian?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer772435874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16562908224120383750"><br/>ALL I'M ASKIN' FOR IS TO HAVE PENRYN TURN INTO AN ANGEL SO THEY COULD HAVE CHILDREN THAT WOULDN'T EAT/TERRORIZE MAN KIND<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/637250.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>P.S. ever since the 2nd book I've been eating peanut butter non-stop, and I didn't even like peanut butter before...LOL<br/><br/>*follow for more reviews :)</span>

<div id="review_1277790980" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277790980" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1277790980?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=same-old-same-old">same-old-same-old</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=apocalypse">apocalypse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=hero-boring">hero-boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=awful-writing">awful-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=awful-love-interest">awful-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=rubbish">rubbish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=used-to-like-heroine">used-to-like-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah-romance">blah-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=heroine-is-a-cow">heroine-is-a-cow</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1277790980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9641904908257404518"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>What a disappointing finale, it was so generic what with Penryn's constant swooning and angsting over Raffe whilst her sister and the world were imploding around her, her nauseating romance with Raffe was all that mattered to her. I really thought this series would stand out from the rest of the YA crap - even though <i>World After</i> was rubbish, <i>Angelfall</i> had a lot going for it and I was expecting the same from this. Unfortunately, when it came to down to it, <i>End of Days</i> was another YA serie</span>
  <span id="freeText9641904908257404518" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />What a disappointing finale, it was so generic what with Penryn's constant swooning and angsting over Raffe whilst her sister and the world were imploding around her, her nauseating romance with Raffe was all that mattered to her. I really thought this series would stand out from the rest of the YA crap - even though <i>World After</i> was rubbish, <i>Angelfall</i> had a lot going for it and I was expecting the same from this. Unfortunately, when it came to down to it, <i>End of Days</i> was another YA series in which the focus was mainly on the lame romance. <br /><br />-The story was somehow both a mess and annoyingly straightforward: Penryn and Raffe drifted here and there, they tried to find a way to beat Uriel and stop his fake apocalypse and bid for power, there was some fighting and weird creatures, and then an anti-climactic showdown, and that was pretty much it. <br />I couldn't fully immerse into the story as the motivations/reasons behind what Uriel was doing felt weak and unclear. Then there were the masses of angels who acted like brain dead sheep, what with them orchestrating an apocalypse and almost wiping out the human race without actually being 100% certain that that was what they were meant to do. Their leader (Gabriel) was suspiciously killed and then power-hungry-politician Uriel started to take over and call all the shots, yet none of the angels were suspicious about Uriel's sudden take over and quest for Gabriel's job/power. Why did they not question his motives? Why didn't they investigate Gabriel's convenient death? Why were they such sheep? Why was there no dissent when it came to killing off all the humans? Ugh, it was all so nonsensical<br /><br />-I was so bored of Penryn's mundane thoughts, her monologuing about how sad her life was and how Raffe wouldn't fuck her was boring to read. She didn't have one original or genuinely selfless thought. I can't believe I used to actually like Penryn, in this she was nothing but a desperate-pervy-loser who cared more about herself and the guy she'd known for a few months than her traumatised sister and the rest of humanity.<br /><br />-I couldn't stand Penryn's non-stop fangirling of Raffe, every other sentence she was banging on about how sexy he looked or how he made her girly parts tingle. Raffe was all that mattered to her. Never mind, her brutally tortured 7 year old sister who was slowly starving to death or the war and apocalypse around her, the only things on her mind were Raffe's sexy abs and hot wings.<br /><br />-What the hell happened to Penryn?! She was a normal enough character in the first book but she turned into a rapey, desperate, ugly fucker in this. She practically molested Raffe in the first few chapters, the mad cow maneuvered him in his sleep so he'd be touching her nipples. What the fuck?! UGH, UGH, UGH. I HATED HER. ALL RESPECT LOST.<br /><br />-Penryn really didn't understand the word 'no'. She kept pawing at Raffe and slobbering all over him even when he repeatedly told her to back the fuck off. She was a desperate, disgusting grade A pervert. <br /><br />-Penryn used to be somewhat smart, but she lost all her intelligence when she fell for Raffe. She let herself be manipulated and used for the most pathetic of reasons. She was seriously TSTL with Beliel, she knew he was manipulative but she still let herself be tricked by him, all so she could spy on more of Raffe's memories. The silly cow's actions probably resulted in the deaths of dozens of humans, those hellions she released must have killed a few people when they escaped, but that thought never crossed her thick, selfish mind. <br /><br />-I had to laugh at Raffe finally giving in to Penryn's desperation and hornyness, the poor guy seemed defeated by the whole thing and no doubt gave in because he didn't know what else to do. Raffe/Penryn's relationship was so one sided, by the end it really did feel like Raffe was only with Penryn because he felt obliged to be with her. There was very little emotion and affection on his side, he just halfheartedly decided to get with her because he was vulnerable and lost and had no idea what else to do. <br /><br />-Why was Paige the chosen one when it came to the locusts? How could she control them? Where did that power and ability to come from? Did Doc engineer it that way? If so, how? And why Paige?<br /><br />-Layla's off-page turn around was awfully convenient. One minute she was evil and happily experimenting on humans, the next she was little miss helpful. Naturally, her turn around just so happened to coincide with Raffe and Penryn needing assistance with their unique medical issues.<br /><br />-How did Penryn's mum manage to survive? Surely her insanity would make it difficult for her to successfully navigate herself in a post apocalyptic world? How did she manage to turn into such an ace strategist and a military mastermind??<br /><br />-Raffe's sword suddenly having the ability to transport his super-warriors to the present day was a total deus ex machina. There was never any hint that the sword could do that, it only ever showed memories, but out of nowhere it was able to transport people through time and space. It was unbelievably contrived.<br /><br />-Why would an eons old archangel who has seen and experienced so much be remotely interested in an insufferable teenage girl? What did he see in Penryn? I know she was meant to be brave and selfless (even though she was actually nothing like that), but would that seriously make an old, powerful angel feel all mushy and lovey-dovey for her? He must have met loads of women who were far more braver and more brilliant than her yet for some unknown reason Penryn was the one he halfheartedly fell for. Ridiculous.<br /><br />-Who the hell were the angels? Were they just another race from a different world or were they actually real angels? If they were real angels then wouldn't they have been in heaven or close to god or something? Wouldn't they be religious? Wouldn't most of them be inherently good or at least fair? How did they even get to Earth from their world? If they were really angels wouldn't they have been punished for killing innocents and having a hand in causing an apocalypse? When the angels were living in their own world what were they doing? What sort of lives they did live? Did they have cities and jobs and families? Were they able to have kids with other angels? If they were all born/made warriors then who were they fighting in all those eons they were away from Earth? Were they just training all that time? <br /><br />-So Gabriel was lying about everything? It wasn't very clear but it was kind of suggested that he wasn't actually a messenger of god and that angels in general weren't god's army, that they were just another species from a different world. It was frustrating that there was little clarity on Gabriel and the angels and the world they came from. Why did Gabriel lie about nephilim being monsters? Was he a purist or something or did he hate humans and want no interbreeding? Also, the angels who did break the law about sexing humans didn't even end up in hell, they were just sent to another world where they were tortured. Did Gabriel lie for the power or control or something? There weren't any satisfying reasons to all of Gabriel's rules and lies when it was the cause of pretty much all the bad that had happened in the world.<br />I needed more information about the origins and driving force behind all that had happened. <br /><br />-Why did the angels (except for a select few) have no personalities? Why did some of them have empathy and compassion and the rest didn't? Why did they only want to fight and kill? Why were they so eager to kill humans? I know they thought it was their duty, but why were there so gleeful about killing off a whole species? Was I just meant to believe they were warriors who loved war because that's just how they were? Was I supposed to just accept that the majority of them were evil yet a handful were able to show compassion and remorse?<br /><br />-Where were all the female characters? Apart from Penryn's mum and sister, there were no other significant female characters. Was the author afraid to add a female character who wasn't related to Paige and who could also hold her own? Penryn was yet again the only girl allowed to hang out with the guys. The author managed to introduce loads of male characters, but she seemed to have trouble bringing in females who had speaking roles and who were in the thick of all the decisions and actions. <br /><br />-Why were the 'Daughters of Men' such a temptation when there were female angels who must have been far more superior? Angels were perfect in every way so why would they want human women when they could have their own far superior women? Did angels even have sex and procreate? Because there were no parents or siblings between the angels, they were all unrelated. What was angel society and structure and family like?!<br /><br />-Where were all the female angels? There was only Laylah and she was a duplicitous-opportunistic-nutbag who didn't even appear on page. Where were the rest of them? If the angel race were meant to be warriors, why wouldn't the female angels be in the thick of the action as well? Were they just at home in their own world making sandwiches in the kitchen despite being part of a fearsome warrior race and being old enough to hold their own? As if.<br /><br />-Didn't like Dee or Dum in this, their dialogue was trying too hard to be funny, their snarky comments and interactions with Penryn and each other were so forced. <br /><br />-Why did the Watchers talk like modern teenagers? They were super old and lived in the olden days and hadn't even experienced modern times. So why didn't they talk how people used to talk centuries/millenia ago?<br /><br />-What was with Penryn's vault in which she stuffed all of her thoughts?! Every time it was mentioned I felt like punching her, it was so irritating to read.<br /><br />-How convenient that two major plot points were sorted out off page, Leylah fixing Raffe's wings and then fixing Paige's whatever the hell was wrong with her. It was irritating that the problems Paige/Raffe faced for two books were quickly dealt with and glossed over in a brief sentence or two. <br /><br />-A talent show? Really? An apocalypse was going on and Penryn and co decided it was good idea to host a talent show minutes before their final showdown. I know it was meant to be a showcase of humanity and all that rubbish, but it just came across as silly and cringey.<br /><br />-The only characters I felt connected to were Belial and Paige, everyone else were either soulless, unrealistic, insufferable, or a caricature. I didn't think I'd end up rooting for for Belial when he was such a heartless-murdering-psychopath, but getting some insight into his history made me rather like him. I didn't blame him for becoming twisted and hateful when he lost everything and was abandoned and betrayed by his so called brothers. Yes, I know he would have done the same thing if one of his brothers had been the gateway, but that didn't make what happened to him any less fucked up and wrong. <br />Poor Paige, hated by everyone for something she had no control over. It was only her mum who supported her and loved her unconditionally. Penryn was still an utter bitch to her, there were never any moments (like in book 1) where Penryn's love for her shone through. Nope, Penryn only cared about her precious Raffe. She should have focused on her sister and helped her through all the trauma she'd been through, but apparently ogling Raffe was more important to her. Bitch.<br /><br />-I hated Raffe/Penryn getting together at the end, it was so predictable and cheesy. Why can't one YA series finish with the teenage heroine being single and ready to date around? Why did she have to be practically married by the end? Also, how the hell will Raffe/Penryn have a healthy and happy relationship when Raffe's immortal? There's no way they'd be able to survive as a couple once Penryn starts to age. Penryn would end up bitter and resentful of Raffe's youth. Not to mention Raffe would no doubt treat Penryn more like a grandma than a lover as she grew older. Their relationship made no sense.<br /><br />-What was with all that Michael nonsense? He was so against being the leader of angels that he did NOTHING when his angels were destroying an entire world, but at the end we were just meant to believe that he'd finally get his act together? That he'd just shrug off all his issues and put down his cup of tea and grudgingly accept the job as angel-leader? Really? After doing jack all when millions were being killed, he would suddenly decide to put on his big boy knickers and take charge? Ugh, nonsensical and ridiculous.<br /><br />-I couldn't help but scoff at Penryn and co's secret weapons against the angels: sharks, bright lights, and rock music. No joke.<br /><br />-The ending was rushed with the fight at the bridge and Raffe/the messengers sending all the angels home, after all that had happened it all seemed too neat and easy.<br /><br />-The writing was generic and mediocre, I don't think I went a page without rolling my eyes. Some random quotes I hated (there were so many to choose from):<br /><br />1. <i>Wearing a backpack this way might not look great on someone else, but on him, it looks like a fitted piece of military gear strapped tight to his broad chest.</i><br /><br />Ugh, of course Raffe can pull anything off because he's just so damn sexy. And naturally, Penryn can't stop ogling him, no matter how inappropriate it is, (what with all the pain and misery surrounding her).<br /><br />2. <i>All I feel is the kiss. All I am is Raffe’s girl.</i><br /><br />Penryn wasn't her own person, she was Raffe's girl throughout the book (even though he didn't want her to be). It was Raffe this and Raffe that and ooh, I wonder how Raffe's feeling?<br /><br />3. <i>Despite Raffe’s supporters being outnumbered, they are the toughest, fiercest, most skilled fighters.</i><br /><br />Of course Raffe had the best team ever. How else could he be the quintessential Gary Stu without being the bestest and sexiest and most skilled guy ever, and in extension all his people have to be the bestest too. Ugh.<br /><br />4. <i>‘And everybody thinks you’re both hot,’ says Dee.<br />I scoff. ‘Now I know you’re full of it.’<br />‘You’re seriously going to tell us you haven’t noticed the way guys look at you?’<br />‘What guys? What are you talking about?’<br />They exchange glances. ‘Girl,’ says Dee, ‘even before your latest stunt, you were becoming the most requested fighter of all our events. Butt-kicking girls have always been smokin’ hot, but in the postapocalyptic world we live in, the hottest thing around is a sword-wielding, angel-slaying, foulmouthed—’</i><br /><br />Wow, a YA heroine that's not only a speshul snowflake but also the hottest and desired girl around? There's something I've never read before! Heaven forbid, a YA heroine who is normal looking and doesn't have countless guys getting wet over her. <br /><br />4. <i>His snowy wings are wide and frame his statuesque body perfectly. The edges of his feathers are downy, giving him a soft glow in the light.<br />I still can’t believe he has his wings back. They look amazing on him. Perfect in every way.</i><br /><br />Those were Penryn's pathetic fangirly thoughts a couple of minutes after she nearly died. Because that's what people do when they nearly die, get swoony and sappy and descriptive over someone else's looks.<br /><br />5. <i>‘Look, I know that we’re from different worlds and different people. But I've realized that it doesn't matter.’</i><br /><br />Naturally, all the many issues and obstacles between Penryn/Raffe's relationships weren't even discussed, everything was brushed under the carpet because True Love conquers all. Ugh.<br /><br /><br />I could go on forever about how bad <i>End of Days</i> was, but I've banged on long enough. It was rubbish. No doubt YA lovers and Raffe fangirls will love this, but I needed more than the usual uninspired, generic YA story/character/relationships, plus the broody-sexy-old-enough-to-be-a-great-great-great-etc-granddad-angel-with-perfect-abs-hero did nothing for me. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9641904908257404518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17692969238910511708"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429899657i/14641688.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Actual Rating: </b> 4.5 stars<br/><br/><strong>I came in without any expectation and went home with so much more than I gambled for. I ended up being such a good fan. </strong>Most trilogies usually start with a bang, but when it comes to the conclusion, it becomes a train wreck. Susan Ee surpassed that wildest expectation without even trying.<br/><br/>End of Days follows shortly after where World After left it off, Penryn and Raffe are trying to find a doctor that could stitch back Raffe’s angel wings and to find a cure for her sister</span>
  <span id="freeText17692969238910511708" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429899657i/14641688.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Actual Rating: </b> 4.5 stars<br><br><strong>I came in without any expectation and went home with so much more than I gambled for. I ended up being such a good fan. </strong>Most trilogies usually start with a bang, but when it comes to the conclusion, it becomes a train wreck. Susan Ee surpassed that wildest expectation without even trying.<br><br>End of Days follows shortly after where World After left it off, Penryn and Raffe are trying to find a doctor that could stitch back Raffe’s angel wings and to find a cure for her sister Paige. They are on the run. And angels are trying to unleash a civil war that could extinct the human race. Will Penryn and Raffe work together or against each other?<br><br>From what I gathered from all the apocalyptic novels I’ve read, they are usually intense and can be very boring. <strong>Susan Ee redefines this genre. She takes the banal aspect and turn it into something unbelievable fun.</strong> I was laughing, swooning, my knees are buckling, I was getting emotional with the characters. All these fervor are all over me.<br><br><strong>The characters are enthralling and well written. </strong>When I read stories, one of the most important things I highly regard is the portrayal of its characters. I look for something authentic. And oh boy, this bunch of characters are so fun to read even the <strong>
  <em>despicable ones.</em>
</strong> Though I have to say, Penryn, Raffe, her mom, Paige and Beliel are my favorites.<br><br><strong>The romance will have everyone moaning. </strong>It. Is. Everything. And. More.<br><br>Favorite Quote:<br><br>“If you’re worried about pervs breaking into the house, it’s not going to make a difference whether I’m in this outfit or in baggy jeans or sweatshirt. Either they’re decent human beings or they’re not. Their actions are on them.”<br><br>“It’ll be tough for them to take any action while I’m plummeting their faces. Disrespect will not be tolerated.”<br><br>End of Days is not to be missed. Fans of Susan Ee will certainly won’t be disappointed in this swashbuckling conclusion.<br><br>Review also posted at <a href="http://youngadulthollywood.com/books/yah-book-review-end-of-days-by-susan-ee/#.VUPOqPlViko" rel="nofollow noopener">Young Adult Hollywood</a>. Listen to my fanmix for End of Days in <a href="https://8tracks.com/rykemeadows/end-of-days" rel="nofollow noopener">8tracks</a>. See the full tracklist in <a href="http://daisycalloway.tumblr.com/post/115255692912/end-of-days-l-listen-were-at-war-on-the" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr.</a></span>

<div id="review_1249845058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249845058" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249845058?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249845058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8720864568601074366">I tried to wait for the crushing disappointment to dissipate a bit before writing this review, so at least you won't have to listen to me rant like a lunatic.<i> Much.</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434824015ra/15267172.gif' width='370' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Was this a bad book? Ehhhhhhh.<br/>It just<i> wasn't anything like</i> what I expecting.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434824111ra/15267183.gif' width='370' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ok, my biggest problem with this was that literally <b>NONE</b> of the questions I had were answered. <br/><i>
  <b>NONE!</b>
</i><br/>So if you go into <b>End of Days</b> thinking that you're going to find out about the origin of the angles, who/what they really are, and whether or not they're r</span>
  <span id="freeText8720864568601074366" style="display:none">I tried to wait for the crushing disappointment to dissipate a bit before writing this review, so at least you won't have to listen to me rant like a lunatic.<i> Much.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434824015ra/15267172.gif" width="370" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Was this a bad book? Ehhhhhhh.<br>It just<i> wasn't anything like</i> what I expecting.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434824111ra/15267183.gif" width="370" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, my biggest problem with this was that literally <b>NONE</b> of the questions I had were answered. <br><i>
  <b>NONE!</b>
</i><br>So if you go into <b>End of Days</b> thinking that you're going to find out about the origin of the angles, who/what they really are, and whether or not they're really talking to God? Have they been duped by some huge conspiracy? How about Penryn's mom? Did she have some prior contact with angels in the past that somehow drove her mad? Is that how she knows about the rotten eggs? Was she maybe not as crazy as we all thought? Why did the sword allow Penryn to pick it up? Was there something<i> more</i> to her? Why is Paige so different from everyone else that they experimented on? <br>Forget it. You'll get hints of half-answers. Nothing else.<br>If anything, you'll have <i>more</i> questions when this is over. And a big reason that I was so friggin excited to get my hands on this, was that I (mistakenly) believed that between the pages of this little novel, I'd be rewarded for my dedication to this trilogy.<br><b>No rewards for Anne!</b><i> *sobs*</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434824312ra/15267208.gif" width="370" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, if nothing else, Raffe is back for the majority of the book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434824402ra/15267223.gif" width="380" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And at least the romance was well done, right?<br><b>Bzzzzt! Wrong!</b><br>I can only describe the romance &amp; subsequent make-out sessions as <i>
  <b>grody to the max</b>
</i>.<br><i>What? Do kids these days not say that anymore?</i><br>Fine. Then I found everything about those two disturbing in this book. See, once again, I assumed that <i>this</i> book was going to somehow <i>fix</i> things. You know, made the ginormous thousand year age gap acceptable in some way. Or maybe one of them becomes mortal or immortal...<i>
  <b>something!</b>
</i><br>GIVE ME SOMETHING! <br>Alas, no. Get used to disappointment, kids.<br><b>But (maybe) worse than that was the awkwardly creepy love scenes.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434824598ra/15267244.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I could have lived my whole life without reading about those two grinding while he flies her around searching for Hellions. <br><b>Dry humping?</b><i> Really?!</i><br>Maybe I've been out of the 'clothes on' game too long, but when the hell did dry humping make a comeback? I mean, come on!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434825324ra/15267357.gif" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I <i>really</i> could have gone without the scene where she puts his hand on her boob while he's sleeping next to her.<br><b>Unacceptable Creeper Behavior! Swerve to avoid!</b><br>Was that supposed to be <i>ok</i> simply because she's a <i>girl</i>? It's not! It's not ok! How are we supposed to teach our boys that this is the kind of thing that will land your ass in jail, if there's some weird double standard for girls? How well would that scene have played out in anyone's head if she had woken up to find him using her hand to rub his junk?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434825471ra/15267402.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alright. Whatever. Maybe I'm one of the few people who didn't lurve the end of this trilogy.<br>Other than the gripes I already talked about, the last thing is that I never really got <i>into</i> this story the way I did the other two books. It may have been because I kept <i>waiting</i> for answers to happen. And without those, this book fell really flat for me.<br>But. It's not a horribly written novel. I finished it in a day, and while I wasn't in love with anything about it, I can't honestly say that it was The Worst Book Evah, either.<br>It was (for me) a middle-of-the-road kind of story, with an ending that felt rushed and unfinished.<br><br>Also reviewed for:<br><div>
  <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2015/07/review-end-of-days-penryn-end-of-days-3.html" title="Addicted 2 Heroines" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412937777i/11444542.jpg" alt="Addicted 2 Heroines" width="100%" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>
  <a data-text-id="8720864568601074366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1112758457" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1112758457" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1112758457?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/37643269-end-of-days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-dystopian">fantasy-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=everyone-loved-it-but-me">everyone-loved-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=the-end-of-the-world-as-we-know-it">the-end-of-the-world-as-we-know-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=hot-guys-alphas-rawr">hot-guys-alphas-rawr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=maybe-its-just-me">maybe-its-just-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1112758457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17561097599189852888"><b>That ending.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431555825ra/14848105.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A part of me wants to give this five stars and another part of me wants to give it one star, so I guess I'll settle on three stars.<br/><br/><b>Action, Pacing, Plot: Five stars.</b> ★★★★★<br/><b>Writing and Supporting Characters: Four stars.</b> ★★★★<br/><b>World-Building: Three stars.</b> ★★★<br/><b>Penryn: Two Stars.</b> ★★<br/><b>Romance, Resolution, and That Ending: One star. Pffft.</b> ★<br/><br/><u>Action, Pacing, Plot, Writing.</u> Obviously, I didn't have issues with these things. I thought the pacing was much improved over World After. There is pretty muc</span>
  <span id="freeText17561097599189852888" style="display:none"><b>That ending.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431555825ra/14848105.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A part of me wants to give this five stars and another part of me wants to give it one star, so I guess I'll settle on three stars.<br><br><b>Action, Pacing, Plot: Five stars.</b> ★★★★★<br><b>Writing and Supporting Characters: Four stars.</b> ★★★★<br><b>World-Building: Three stars.</b> ★★★<br><b>Penryn: Two Stars.</b> ★★<br><b>Romance, Resolution, and That Ending: One star. Pffft.</b> ★<br><br><u>Action, Pacing, Plot, Writing.</u> Obviously, I didn't have issues with these things. I thought the pacing was much improved over World After. There is pretty much always something going on in this book. The story overall was a good one to wrap up this trilogy.<br><br><u>Supporting Characters.</u> I really love Paige. God, I love her. She may be my favorite character in the whole series. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Paige as Queen of the Locusts was just awesome. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Penryn's Mom is also fantastic in this. Shining moments. I loved Beliel in this and you get to see a COMPLETELY different side to him. There are also some new characters introduced - the Watchers - and they were good. I didn't quite like Dee/Dum as much as the previous books. Their dialogue felt forced and not fresh or funny to me. <br><br><u>World Building and Resolution.</u> I'll group these together since they are similiar. Although I did like the inclusion of the pit, there really wasn't a whole lot added and I was very disappointed with all the things the author never explained about this world. Seriously. Some things were left so vague or simply ignored. The ending was so incredibly rushed and felt slapped together.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ ↓ WTH was up with Layla in this and all the stuff she did off-page??? Big disappointment. She fixes Raffe's wings and fixes Paige but we don't get to see that at all.<br>↓ Where were all the other female angels? Were there no warrior females? It kind of feels like maybe the author only wanted one bad-ass female character around the angels - Penryn. <br>↓ Why were the angels on earth to begin with? <br>↓ Where did they come from? Another planet, another dimension?<br>↓ Raffe suddenly admits the Watchers children were not monsters but perfectly healthy???!!! Oh really. That seems like an easy way for the author to enable Penryn and Raffe to have babies and a cheesy HEA. Funny how that changed suddenly. Why didn't he tell Penryn that to begin with? Probably because the author changed her mind and decide to go with the predictable romance HEA. <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431570273ra/14849674.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Penryn.</u> I did not like her as much in this. I know a lot of people felt that scene around 9% was steamy, but it was not sexy to me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Raffe was asleep and she basically molested him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She was really angsty in this about Raffe and it got annoying. <br><br><u>Romance and The Ending.</u> I will go ahead and group these two together. There was much more romance in this and I didn't like the way it was done. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When their romance was unrequited, it worked for me. Penryn is <b>17</b>. I don't care how bad-ass and smart she is, Raffe is <b>thousands of years old.</b> The insta-love Penryn had for Raffe worked because he was a hot angel and it was the end of the world and yes, they formed an unusual bond because of extraordinary and traumatic circumstances. HOWEVER, it doesn't work the other way around. Raffe is used to being in traumatic circumstances and war. He would not fall insta-in-love with a 17 year old he just met two months ago. <b><u>And choose to stay on earth and not go back with his people.</u></b>The ending was the typical expected HEA. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Overall, I was very much caught up in the book and was able to overlook the unanswered questions and stuff <u>until that ending.</u> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431570273ra/14849675.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A part of me is angry, but I feel conflicted because I really did enjoy most of the book. I think if the ending hadn't been SO CHEESY, I would have overlooked more of the issues I had with it.<br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/78704-saucy-wenches-book-club" rel="nofollow noopener">Saucy Wenches</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a> groups.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17561097599189852888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1736866818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736866818" />
    <a title="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog"><img alt="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484605631p2/44673856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1736866818?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" href="/user/show/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog">Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736866818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5318338802630369460"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466616465i/19500517.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466042213i/19431593.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>➦Ok, so... perhaps the most <b>IMPORTANT</b> thing I've learned from this book is <b>how to ride an angel.</b> Take your mind out of the gutter, people!
