<div id="review_702238001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/702238001" />
    <a title="Danielle (Love at First Page)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page"><img alt="Danielle (Love at First Page)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578285312p2/1312450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/702238001?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle (Love at First Page)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle (Love at First Page)" href="/user/show/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page">Danielle (Love at First Page)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444778557" href="/book/show/13638020-end-of-days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=so-otp-it-hurts">so-otp-it-hurts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=genre-young-adult">genre-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=fantasy-scifi-paranormal">fantasy-scifi-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=favorites-young-adult">favorites-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=own-kindle-book">own-kindle-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer702238001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16361684222434137251"><b>4-4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>It's so hard to let this series go! I've adored Penryn & the End of Days ever since reading the first book, and now I can say without a doubt that it's a favorite of mine. Each and every book has been incredibly fun and emotionally satisfying. I have to admit, though, that when Susan Ee first announced that the series would be three books long, the prayer candles started to come out. I was terrified about what would happen to my ship in <i>End of Days</i>; would it be the end of them? *deep </span>
  <span id="freeText16361684222434137251" style="display:none"><b>4-4.5 stars</b><br /><br />It's so hard to let this series go! I've adored Penryn &amp; the End of Days ever since reading the first book, and now I can say without a doubt that it's a favorite of mine. Each and every book has been incredibly fun and emotionally satisfying. I have to admit, though, that when Susan Ee first announced that the series would be three books long, the prayer candles started to come out. I was terrified about what would happen to my ship in <i>End of Days</i>; would it be the end of them? *deep breaths*<br /><br />But let me back up...<br /><br />If you have not yet read the brilliance that is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>, I will tell you what you are missing.<br /><b>*Angels.<br />*Post-apocalyptic setting. End of the world. Angels vs. humanity. Angels vs. angels.<br />*A remarkably tough, resourceful, and downright loveable heroine.<br />*A cocky but sexy love interest who also happens to be an archangel.<br />*<i>Holy sexual tension.</i><br />*Banter.<br />*SHIP RUINERS.<br />*More banter.<br />*Creepy, gruesome creatures straight out of hell.<br />*A fun supporting cast, including a crazy mother who you will love to hate but then come to have the oddest respect for.<br />*Tons of action alongside swoon-worthy romance.<br />*A sword named Pooky Bear.</b><br /><br />In this third and final book, it seems humanity is holding its last breath. The angels have released an apocalyptic nightmare, and Penryn is left wondering which side Raffe will be on. While the angels' infighting surges, Penryn struggles to make sense of herself as a leader and Raffe must form a new strategy to bring peace between angels and humans. When the final battle draws near, will they be standing together or apart?<br /><br />Me being me, I was <i>extremely</i> nervous about the fate of Penryn and Raffe. The world is coming to an end, what with the angels declaring Judgment Day and willing to obliterate humanity for their own nefarious purposes, but I just needed to know one thing: are Penryn and Raffe endgame?! <br /><br />Susan Ee doesn't make it easy. <i>End of Days</i> is her sexiest book yet. There are kisses that will leave you breathless and wanting more. There are moments between Penryn and Raffe that had my heart squeezing tight, especially when they allowed themselves to be vulnerable. But... there's so much standing between them, beginning and ending with the fact that he's an angel and she's a Daughter of Man. How could they realistically stay together? An almost impossible question, so I was eager to see how, if at all, Susan Ee would answer it. But if one thing is certain, it's how well Raffe and Penryn work together as a team. I know I'm not the only one who wishes couples in YA books (especially fantasy/dystopian series) actually communicated and demonstrated why they are so good together, and that's exactly what Penryn and Raffe do. The chemistry is there, but so is the way they <i>show</i> how much they care and how well-suited they are together. I appreciate the amount of time we get with them in this last book, seeing them work in harmony and in complete trust. They are a true team. <br /><br />Like the first two books, <i>End of Days</i> is a great mixture of plot and characters. Penryn is an amazing heroine, a girl who has had to grow up too fast (even before the apocalypse) but who still longs with a teenager's heart. Her strength always inspired me, and it's paired so well with her warrior love interest. You wouldn't think a young girl could keep someone like Raffe on his toes, but she so does. Their verbal sparring is priceless. Raffe is pretty much temptation incarnate, with his immense strength and sarcastic demeanor. But I love his growth, especially in this last book, when he's faced with the choice of his angel brethren and the girl he's fallen for. Raffe, as an angel, is not meant to be alone, but who will he seek comfort from?<br /><br />The other cast of characters have always taken back seat to the Raffe and Penryn show, but they are a compelling mix. Penryn's mom, especially, has more depth than I had originally given her credit for. She's crafty and clever, if a bit crazy, and her antics are quite humorous at times, too. As you can expect, there's an epic showdown at the end, and I am super pleased with how these events unfold. Susan Ee makes the whole story line not only chock full of action but believable, too. (I was surprised with the way she plays with time at one point in the book. It's done so effectively, especially because I wasn't expecting something of the sort.) My main complaint would be that I wanted just a little bit more at the end. One more chapter with these beloved characters.<br /><br />I can't believe this series has come to a close, but I know I will be remembering Penryn and Raffe's story for years to come. If the apocalypse ever does come around, well, I'll try to be as tough-minded and strong-willed as Penryn, and maybe hope there's a warrior angel in store for me? ;) (Books have clearly ruined me for life...) Start this series if you haven't yet, but if you have I don't think you'll be disappointed in this epic conclusion. <br /><br /><i>***Major thanks and hugs to <a href="http://nicksbookblog93.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Nick</a> who let me borrow her ARC!***</i><br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="http://www.loveatfirstpage.org/2015/04/30/arc-review-end-of-days/" rel="nofollow noopener">Love at First Page</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16361684222434137251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1299070999" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299070999" />
    <a title="Sophia." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6520961-sophia"><img alt="Sophia." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322479535p2/6520961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1299070999?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia." href="/user/show/6520961-sophia">Sophia.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=awful">awful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=clumsy-symbolism">clumsy-symbolism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=doesnt-make-any-sense">doesnt-make-any-sense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=epic-fail">epic-fail</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=too-cliche">too-cliche</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=huge-disappointment">huge-disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=flaws-in-the-concept">flaws-in-the-concept</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1299070999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7110179738758294498">Man, that trilogy was such a trainwreck. Where was the editor for this book? What was he doing? And why didn’t he tell Ee that a chapter should be longer than TWO PAGES? <br/><br/>It was so poorly written, it actually managed to make me cringe and put down the book in disgust several times, which I didn’t think was possible. <br/><br/>So in the second book, there was hardly any romance at all, but in this one, the romance is suddenly everywhere and so abruptly sexual it was intensely awkward. What’s with the sleepi</span>
  <span id="freeText7110179738758294498" style="display:none">Man, that trilogy was such a trainwreck. Where was the editor for this book? What was he doing? And why didn’t he tell Ee that a chapter should be longer than TWO PAGES? <br /><br />It was so poorly written, it actually managed to make me cringe and put down the book in disgust several times, which I didn’t think was possible. <br /><br />So in the second book, there was hardly any romance at all, but in this one, the romance is suddenly everywhere and so abruptly sexual it was intensely awkward. What’s with the sleeping-together scene? In what universe is it okay to move someone’s arm while they’re sleeping to have them touch your breasts? What if the roles were reversed? I’m pretty sure everyone would go nuts if it'd been a guy moving a sleeping girl’s arm so that she’d touch his balls. <br /><br />Penryn changed. I think the first and second book were all about sending the message that even if there was an attraction between Penryn and Raffe, it could not be *more* important than what was going on. Penryn just didn't have the <i>time</i>, what with Paige’s abduction in the first book and dealing with the “world after” in the second book. But in the third book, even though nothing is resolved regarding the state of the world, Penryn’s priorities somehow shift and literally all she can think about is Raffe. The kissing scenes were weird (like why would you repeatedly use the word “wet”) and Penryn’s attitudes were cringe-worthy:<br /><blockquote>‘And everybody thinks you’re hot,’ says Dee.<br />I scoff. ‘Now I know you’re full of it.’<br />‘You’re seriously going to tell us you haven’t noticed the way guys look at you?’<br />‘What guys? What are you talking about?’<br />They exchange glances. ‘Girl,’ says Dee, ‘even before your latest stunt, you were becoming the most requested fighter of all our events. Butt-kicking girls have always been smokin’ hot, but in the postapocalyptic world we live in, the hottest thing around is a sword-wielding, angel-slaying, foulmouthed—’</blockquote><br />That excerpt, right there - it's responsible for me knocking off one star. Please. Like we need another mindless, stupid heroin who's doesn't know she's pretty! *eye roll* <br /><br />And what is this?<br /><blockquote>“He stares deep into my eyes. It makes me squirm but also makes my heart flutter like a schoolgirl’s. Oh, wait. I am a schoolgirl. I blink a few times, wondering if that’s how I’m supposed to bat my eyelashes.<br />‘What are you doing?’<br />‘What?’ Ugh. I suck at this.<br />‘Are you batting your lashes at me?’<br />‘What, me? No, of course not.’<br />He squints his eyes suspiciously at me. ‘This is awkward.’<br />‘Yes, it is.”</blockquote><br />KILL ME NOW! Who would ever do that? WTF?<br /><br />And sooo <b>many repetitions</b> too: how many times can she say that Raffe’s skin is warm and that she nuzzles in his neck when she flies with him? It felt like Ee copypasted ENTIRE descriptive paragraphs. <br /><br />The biggest problem, and of course that’s what everyone complained about, is the <b>lack of a substantial world building and storyline</b>. Actually, that problem first appeared in the second book and while reading, I could never really tell you what was happening. It wasn't gripping enough for me to stay focused. It was always like this: [Paige is missing or whatever] Raffe and Penryn have to get from point A to point B for obscure reasons, he flies with her, they encounter bad guys, they fight, then they almost lose but oh no wait they survive, and they manage to escape, they go into a random house, some flirting ensues, then they have to go somewhere else, so they leave, and then they fight... This is literally what happened like a dozen times. It was always the same thing. <br /><br />Remember, back when the first book was published and everyone was beaming and saying how for once the author knew her shit and had obviously done solid research on Angels? Yeah, well no, it’s no longer the case. The book got increasingly, unbelievably bad as Penryn does random things like going to the Pit/Hell/whatever with angels that have supposedly been around for millenniums but yet talk like your average 14-year-old Californian girl, and they fight demons that no one can take seriously as they make no sense whatsoever. Other random things happen but no one really knows why, such as Laylah suddenly becoming one of the good guys (while also apparently being the only fucking female in the entire angel world), Paige being able to control the scorpions, a talent show that I have yet to understand… Overall, weak and shallow plotline, and contradictory world building. I swear it sometimes looked like a sixth grader wrote it.<br /><br />There is also a major problem regarding the <b>terrible characterization</b>. There’s not a single well fleshed-out, multi-dimensional character. They’re all cliché and stick to their one descriptive trait : Mom is crazy (did she cause Paige's accident? Was she an abusive mother? Why is she like that?), Raffe is hot, Clara is kind, Obi is a leader, Dee and Dum are “cool” (but really dumbasses), and... wait that’s the whole cast. <br /><br />Also, Paige is supposed to be a main character but really she’s very generic and has about 8 lines of dialogue in the entire trilogy (with well thought-out, constructed lines such as “Hungry” and “Penryn”). <br /><br />The fact that she was now bound to only eat human flesh was interesting and could have led to deep, disturbing discussions. Paige struggles with her new condition at the beginning, and tries desperately to starve herself. That raises interesting points, survival vs humanity, necessity vs morality. And then there's Paige's entourage, and their different reactions, which can only lead to more questions. How far would you be willing to go for someone you love? Would you feed them human victims, if that was the price to pay for them to stay alive? <br /><br />Unfortunately, discussions like these never appear in the book. No one actively adresses Paige's condition. We're stuck in Penryn's head and she never thought about it for more than three lines, she would always go back to Raffe. <br />Penryn keeps saying she’s grown tougher because of the Apocalypse, that she’d do anything for Paige, but once she does rescue her, she fails to take care of her the way one would expect her to. I understand that she would be in denial about Paige’s needs, but you can’t have her ignore that situation in the entire book! Why would she stop her Mom from giving a willing victim to Paige? I kept getting so annoyed at Penryn’s stubbornness to try and feed Paige vegetables (mostly in book 2) when EVERYONE knew what she really needed in order for her to survive. <br /><br />Paige, even though she had potential, grew boring and Ee's problem with repetitions didn't help. How many times were Paige's stitches mentioned? And why is she able to control the monsters? For some dark reason that Ee feels unnecessary to explain, Paige seems to be the key to saving… I don’t know what actually, but you can't throw around random statements like “She’s the Chosen One” and NOT explain, and expect us to move on! What was so special about her? Was it just because she was the last monster-child? Why could Penryn wield an Angel sword? (By the way, I HATED the sword. From its stupid name, to the "dreams" that were a convienent way for the author to do some lazy info-dump). <br /><br />And the angels have got to be the most idiotic species I've ever had the misfortune to read about. I swear, a herd of LLAMAS would be smarter. They mindlessly follow whatever orders they're being given, without ever analyzing their own motives. Where do they live? Do they have a God? Can they have children? As always though, Ee provides no answer at all. <br /><br />And how many times can Penryn ALMOST die but then miraculously find a way out? Since the book is first-person narrated in present tense, you know she can’t die, but that didn’t stop the author from giving us DOZENS of scenes where it seems like Penryn can’t win, and at the last second, something or someone shows up and saves her. It got exasperating. <br /><br />Which brings us to the next problem: the <b>happy ending.</b><br /><br />No one died in this trilogy. Penryn managed to have EVERYTHING and save everyone, and that’s a problem. If you want me to believe that it IS the end of the world, and that they are nearing the Apocalypse, you also have to show me an evident truth: people die. You can't go through hundreds of armed fights without ever getting hurt. She's not wounded a SINGLE time in the entire trilogy. How is it possible? <br /><br />You can’t just write about thousands or even millions of faceless casualties and expect me to care, it doesn’t make me feel anything. Yeah, Obi died but let’s be real, who cared?! <br /><br /><b>Sacrifices should have been made</b>. And I feel like there were three different possibilities for the author : The mom, Paige, or Raffe. Penryn should have lost SOMETHING. For example, the mom could have left and never come back, because that wouldn’t be too unexpected from an insane person. <br /><br />But mostly Paige shouldn’t have been healed, because that’s just too much of a stretch. I don’t think she could be cured from her experiments (I fail to see how cannibalistic cravings can be taken out of someone). Ideally, she should have died. Tough, yes, and I would have been upset, but in a good way. At least it wouldn’t be that sickeningly sweet epilogue that MAKES NO SENSE. Authors have to make sacrifices! It’s inevitable if you want to add depth to the story. Especially if you chose apocalyptic settings, a happy ending is stupid. You can’t have the cake and eat it too. <br /><br />What’s also a huge problem is, of course, Raffe and Penryn’s love story’s outcome. I was truly convinced, up until the middle of the third book, that Ee would stay reasonable and have Raffe leave – which was the ONLY possible solution. I don’t think they should have ended up together, and even if it was frustrating, I was ready to accept it. I would have loved some kind of Peter Pan ending, with Raffe leaving and maybe coming back decades later, and her remembering him vaguely, or better yet, maybe she had been waiting for him to return that whole time. Or even an adult Penryn dating someone who casually says "I swear it's like you have a guardian angel sometimes".<br /><br />So many possibilities to be explored - the classic YA Happily Ever After is only one of them, and it's the weakest of them all! Because goddammit, if you're going to write about an impossible love story set in an apocalyptic world, then okay, but at least have the balls to give it the rightful ending! Yeah, it's tough decision-making but the value of the book and series as a whole would dramatically change altogether!<br /><br />And if Ee really, really couldn’t accept the idea of them being separated, she should have balanced things out by adding in hard dilemmas, such as, an offer for Penryn to join him in the angel world, to the condition that she leaves the human world behind forever. Would she give up on Paige? Now that would have been interesting conflict!<br /><br />But no. At some point there was some random talk about some humans being ancestors of angels and having some kind of angelic blood, and I freaked out because it seemed obvious that Ee was talking about Penryn. Therefore her and Raffe being together could have worked out. But it didn’t even go this far, Raffe just chooses to STAY. No! It makes no sense. You can’t ignore the context, you can’t just conclude by saying “I’ve realized it doesn’t matter.”<br /><br />It does! You’re immortal! She’s SEVENTEEN! How is that ever going to work? What is so complicated in accepting the fact that you're not meant to be together?<br /><br />Of course, there’s all the unanswered questions regarding what exactly Raffe saw in Penryn. Why did he "love" her? Why her? <br /><br />I liked it when Beliel said to Penryn: <br /><blockquote>“You’re in love with him, aren’t you? You think you’re so special. Special enough to catch an archangel’s love. Do you know how many people have thought they could win his love over the centuries? That he’d be loyal to them just as they were loyal to him? You want to know how many human girls he’s gone through? How many hearts do you think have shattered over Raphael, the great archangel?”</blockquote><br />Yes! Listen to that, Penryn! I liked that. It's realistic. But of course there’s a problem when you agree with the villain. <br /><br />Sigh. <br /><br />TO CONCLUDE. <br /><br />I think the series perfectly illustrates how the publishing world can pressure an author into self-sabotaging their own work. I genuinely believe that the first book was great, because it came from Ee as a spontaneous idea and project. She must have worked on it without any sort of pressure, because she was unknown, and it was self-published. I don’t think she expected the book to be as successful as it was, and Publishing Houses, seeing the potential profits, must have put insane pressure on her shoulder to milk the cash cow. I’m talking about turning good books into series, of course. <br /><br />Now where have I seen this before? An example among so many, but it does remind of Stephanie Perkins. She wrote Anna and the French kiss and it was insanely good, and then she had to publish two other books to complete an <b>unnatural trilogy that was forced and made for money</b>. Actually, I think both authors struggled with writer’s block, and both ended up pushing back deadlines – and how can you blame them? It was supposed to be five books, then three, and if I remember correctly, Ee got critisized for snapping at her readers' impatience. I get that, though, expectant readers can be so demanding, so passionate, it's enough to make an author flip. <br /><br />I don’t think Ee knew how she wanted her story to end after Angelfall. I don't think she had enough time to let her draft form and develop. I think she needed more time. She had so much pressure, and probably not a lot of ideas... but that’s how business works. So she wrote those sequels in a very short amount of time... And well – that’s the result. <br /><br />What a shame.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7110179738758294498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Lucia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucia" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia">Lucia</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=5-stars-read">5-stars-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=bookshelves-owned">bookshelves-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer396330521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3293418828137298969"><b>Powerful conclusion to one-of-a-kind series!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431787266i/14866749._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"We are soldiers, Penryn. Legendary warriors willing to make legendary sacrifices. We do not ask. We do not choose."</i>
</blockquote><br/>Since this is the last book in series and I don't want to spoil it for those who haven't read it yet, I'm going to keep my review sweet and short. Keep in mind that End of Days has quite different dynamics than previous instalments. So if you expect another Angefall and World After, you will be disappointed. Once I got used to this di</span>
  <span id="freeText3293418828137298969" style="display:none"><b>Powerful conclusion to one-of-a-kind series!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431787266i/14866749._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"We are soldiers, Penryn. Legendary warriors willing to make legendary sacrifices. We do not ask. We do not choose."</i>
</blockquote><br>Since this is the last book in series and I don't want to spoil it for those who haven't read it yet, I'm going to keep my review sweet and short. Keep in mind that End of Days has quite different dynamics than previous instalments. So if you expect another Angefall and World After, you will be disappointed. Once I got used to this different "drive" (around 30%), I could not put this book down and read it in one sitting. And that is one of the best compliments I can pay to a book. <br><br>End of Days is one of the best stories about survival I have ever read. Humanity, its strengths and weaknesses are the main focus of this book. Author provided a powerful example of the best and the worst that humanity has to offer. It brought tears to my eyes, gave me goosebumps and most importantly it made me feel so much!<br><br>Now that Penryn and the End of Days series is over, I can say that it is most memorable and without the doubt my all time favorite series featuring star-crossed lovers. I think I have never shipped any YA couple as much as I ship Penryn &amp; Raffe. (Only Josh &amp; Sky from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165694067?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">I'll Meet You There</a> compare, but that is a story for another time.) And until the very end of this book I had no idea if Penryn and Raffe would get their HEA or not. Kudos to author for creating such amazing and unforgettable characters!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"History is filled with teenagers who lead the fight. Joan of Arc. Okita Soji, the samurai. Alexander the Great. They were all teenagers when they began leading their armies. I think we’re back to those times again, kid."</i>
</blockquote><br>MORE REVIEWS ON MY BLOG <a href="http://readingismybreathing.blogspot.cz/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Reading Is My Breathing</b>
</a></span>

I love Penryn and Raffe so muuuuuuuuch.<br/>Overall, pretty fantastic trilogy.</span>

<div id="review_1127913463" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1127913463" />
    <a title="Marga " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6418118-marga"><img alt="Marga " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423326869p2/6418118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1127913463?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marga " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marga " href="/user/show/6418118-marga">Marga </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444778557" href="/book/show/13638020-end-of-days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=angels-vampires-werewolves">angels-vampires-werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=fan-freaking-tastic">fan-freaking-tastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>,

<div id="review_1278177081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278177081" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1278177081?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1278177081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5351173241601334577">✬✬✬✬½ Overall Series<br/>✰✰✰✰✰ <a>Angelfall</a><br/>✬✬✬✬½ <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/604420856%E2%80%9D' rel='nofollow noopener'>World After</a><br/>✰✰✰✰ End of Days<br/><br/>Buddy read with a ridiculous number of people at <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a>
</b><br/><br/>End of Days took what I loved in Angelfall and World After and added to it some of the things I missed, more of the stuff I loved and gave it entirely new dimensions.<br/><br/><b>A List of Awesomeness in End of Days:</b><br/><blockquote>✔ - More Romance - <i>OkayIwaswrong</i> (totally sigh worthy trust me) and some YA hot fans-self worthy moments….hint rhymes with <i>missing</i><br/>✔ - Weirder Imagery (</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5351173241601334577" style="display:none">✬✬✬✬½ Overall Series<br>✰✰✰✰✰ <a>Angelfall</a><br>✬✬✬✬½ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/604420856%E2%80%9D" rel="nofollow noopener">World After</a><br>✰✰✰✰ End of Days<br><br>Buddy read with a ridiculous number of people at <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a>
</b><br><br>End of Days took what I loved in Angelfall and World After and added to it some of the things I missed, more of the stuff I loved and gave it entirely new dimensions.<br><br><b>A List of Awesomeness in End of Days:</b><br><blockquote>✔ - More Romance - <i>OkayIwaswrong</i> (totally sigh worthy trust me) and some YA hot fans-self worthy moments….hint rhymes with <i>missing</i><br>✔ - Weirder Imagery (<i>who knew it could be done</i>) it was disturbing and I will never think of hell the same way again.<br>✔ - More Raffe!!! I missed him in World After – <b>WE NEEDED</b> more Penryn/Raffe banter time after World After.<br><br><i>“Might as well fly into the heart of the enemy where the primitive natives can tear me to pieces, sell my body parts for money, and grind the rest to be consumed in teas for sexual potency.”<br>I tighten my arms around his neck. “We’re not that primitive anymore.”<br>He arches his perfect eyebrow at me, sending waves of skepticism.<br>“We have Viagra now.”</i><br><br>✔ - DeeDum antics including a Talent Show AND who would win in a fight between Godzilla and members of Penryn’s entourage. <i>I know who I’d put money on.</i><br>✔- Penryn’s crazy/not-so-crazy mother. Sometimes there is rhyme to her reason and other times…well you’ve read the other books so you know.<br>✔ - #TeamFallen – I’m totally on the Fallen Watchers team.<br>✔ - PAIGE - *sobs* that little girl has been through hell but at least Penryn isn’t afraid of her anymore.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431535347i/14844376._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="273" alt="paige" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✔ - POOKY BEAR – is as epic and awesome as ever with a few new tricks up her sleeve.<br>✔ - Redemption of a character I thought unredeemable.<br>✔ - Angel Elections a fascinating blend of democracy, fighting and survival of the fittest all at the same time.<br>✔ - Crazy creatures and epic battles<br>✔ - AND FINALLY – an ending that I really liked. <i>not perfect I still have so many unanswered questions, but I’m really okay with how the series wrapped up</i> </blockquote><br><br>End of Days starts exactly where World After ended. It is a crazy wild ride from beginning to end and I really don’t think I could have guessed how any of this would play out. Actually I did guess and I was SO SO Wrong, I don’t think a single theory panned out for me except for my one on little Paige. <br><br>Susan Ee gave us some new and fantastical scenes from hell, she bridged new territory with her imaginings of the demon realm and I for one am in awe of it. Just when it got too heavy and too gruesome she tempered it with quick wit and humor to keep it from becoming overwhelming. Plus there was romance….shhhh I know I know, but I loved every touch, kiss and tender moment shared between our star-crossed couple.<br><br>The only reason I deducted a star was there are a few things that either were ignored or didn’t wrap up or I still have a ton of questions about and was left pondering them well after I finished the book. <b>THEY ARE ALL SPOILERS</b>…..do not click on the tag unless you have finished the book<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>If you reply to any of my comments in this section please be sure to spoiler tag them appropriately </i><br><br>① - The immortal/mortal thing not even broached? Raffe totally still immortal, Penryn completely mortal so they get 50 – 60 years together and poof done. It wasn’t even really mentioned. Don’t get me wrong I love that he ended up staying on earth and SUPER LOVE that he took the demon wings back because seriously I thought they were way cooler. But that just seemed a little glossed over and under fleshed out. Layla sorta fixed Paige (vague description) couldn’t she also just randomly added something to Penryn for a little extended life mojo….just saying. <br><br>Also the very end hook up was slightly cheesy…..or maybe that was just me. I wanted possibly a smidgen more on that front.<br><br>② - What the hell happened to all the 666 creatures with their consumed heads? Do they still just hang out in our Ocean or did they go back to the demon plain with the Pit Lord?<br><br>③ - Would Raffe and his watchers really have participated in the Blood Hunt to win? I really wish Penryn would have asked and that Raffe had a different plan in mind. That is quite a big thing to forgive if he was going to decimate all those humans.<br><br>④ - The Nephilim – this is really my smallest thing. Susan Ee totally changed the lore and the Nephilim were harmless and just babies…no monster flesh eating tendencies. Now most humans have a little diluted angle blood in them. Hmmm….was that why Penryn could touch the sword she is a little small bit Angel. <br><br>Mostly that is it. I gave up on the Raffe is millennia old and Penryn is 17 thing a long time ago so it doesn’t bother me…in my head with all of her mom crap and raising Paige she is easily the equivalent of 25. Nothing really bothered me so much that it diminished my overall enjoyment of the story. <br><br>I really wonder if Ee is going to revisit the hellion realm or this world again in future stories. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5351173241601334577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_790014274" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/790014274" />
    <a title="Toni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24617462-toni"><img alt="Toni" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/790014274?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toni" href="/user/show/24617462-toni">Toni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781477829707" href="/book/show/23901077-end-of-days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24617462-toni?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer790014274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10798651900010178923">UPDATE: I lowered my rating (again) because the more I think about the book the less I like how it turned out.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Who wants to go to heaven anymore? There's nothing but angels there.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Since I'm a bit conflicted let's make this review ♛ (positive things) vs. ✖ (well that is pretty self-explanatory).<br/><br/>♛ <b>It wasn't a bad book</b>. While it wasn't as good of a conclusion as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18001518.Dreams_of_Gods_and_Monsters__Daughter_of_Smoke_and_Bone___3_' title='Dreams of Gods and Monsters (Daughter of Smoke and Bone, #3) by Laini Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dreams of Gods and Monsters</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7304203.Shadowfever__Fever___5_' title='Shadowfever (Fever, #5) by Karen Marie Moning' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadowfever</a>, I enjoyed it and I think it concluded some things and left others open in a way that makes</span>
  <span id="freeText10798651900010178923" style="display:none">UPDATE: I lowered my rating (again) because the more I think about the book the less I like how it turned out.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Who wants to go to heaven anymore? There's nothing but angels there.”</i>
</b><br><br>Since I'm a bit conflicted let's make this review ♛ (positive things) vs. ✖ (well that is pretty self-explanatory).<br><br>♛ <b>It wasn't a bad book</b>. While it wasn't as good of a conclusion as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18001518.Dreams_of_Gods_and_Monsters__Daughter_of_Smoke_and_Bone___3_" title="Dreams of Gods and Monsters (Daughter of Smoke and Bone, #3) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreams of Gods and Monsters</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7304203.Shadowfever__Fever___5_" title="Shadowfever (Fever, #5) by Karen Marie Moning" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadowfever</a>, I enjoyed it and I think it concluded some things and left others open in a way that makes sense.<br><br>✖ <b> But it wasn't a very memorable book either</b>. When you read a book in a very short period of time you tend to forget a lot of details. But still, when I read the first two books in a pretty much the same period of time, I remembered a lot of it. <i>Angelfall</i> and <i>World After</i> left me obsessed. <i>End Of Days</i> left me with too little.<br><br>♛ <b> The angels, the locusts, other new creatures,<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[666 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>...I love it</b>. Susan Ee has an imagination and it makes me giddy. <br><br>✖ The whole Pit Lord situation.<br><br>✖ The romance was too much. <b>It also made me cringe.</b><br><br><i> “Josiah looks at me, then back at Raffe. “Does she need to be here?” <br>“Apparently, she does,” says Raffe. “It turns out that she’s the only one I can trust to watch my back.”</i><br><br>✖ Too much of Penryn thinking about Raffe. I like the guy a lot too, but it's the "end of times". Get your shit together.<br><br>♛ <b>The humor</b>. The writing style of these books is full of humor and hilarious characters...<br><br><i>“Might as well fly into the heart of the enemy where the primitive natives can tear me to pieces, sell my body parts for money, and grind the rest to be consumed in teas for sexual potency.” <br>I tighten my arms around his neck. “We’re not that primitive anymore.” He arches his perfect eyebrow at me, sending waves of skepticism. <br>“We have Viagra now.”</i><br><br>♛ <b>...which also brings us to...DUM AND DEE!</b> aka the Fred and George of this series. Dum and Dee might be my favorite characters in the whole book. They are loveable, not to mention endlessly entertaining.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427487016ra/14276342.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>♛ <b> "The mom, the kind monster and me" family dynamic</b>. Both the mum and Paige are complex characters and I loved the relationships in this odd little family play out.<br><br>✖ <b>Me, not caring much for Penryn.</b> I don't adore her character anymore. SHE CHANGED. In a bad way.<br><br>♛ THIS:<br><br><i>“If you're worried about pervs breaking into the house, it's not going to make a difference whether I'm in this outfit or in baggy jeans and a sweatshirt. <b>Either they're decent human beings or they're not. Their actions are on them.</b>” </i><br><br>Important and brilliantly told.<br><br>✖ <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bringing hellions through the sword thing. No, I didn't quite buy it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>♛ THE TALENT SHOW. Best part of the book. Humanity on the page. If I could rate a scene 5 stars, it would be that one.<br><br>♛ Humanity is flawed. All the humans in this book feel fleshed out, even if they get a very short amount of page time. The <i>Penryn and the End Of Days</i> series presents people in their good and their bad in a realistic way even with a world full of angels.<br><br>✖ Anti-climatic. <br><br>✖ <b>Pretty convenient ending.</b><br><br><br>_____________________________________<br><u>28.6</u>: So I obviously didn't read this in May. But now is finally the time.<br>_____________________________________<br><u>6.5.</u> : <b>I GOT IT!</b> I'm going to read it this weekend.<br>_____________________________________<br><b>Guys THE COVER!</b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1423239458l/13638020.jpg" width="300" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh my pretty.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1700745164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1700745164" />
    <a title="sreeja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50309540-sreeja"><img alt="sreeja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598363186p2/50309540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1700745164?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sreeja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sreeja" href="/user/show/50309540-sreeja">sreeja</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50309540-sreeja?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1700745164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18235265839560344032">I’M REALLY SAD THAT THIS IS OVER :(((( this series was spectacular as a whole! This book was great but it did have something about it that did not quite put it up to my expectations. The character development was fantastic, the relationship growth of everyone was great and also THIS BOOK HAD THE CUTEST MOMENTS. I was really devastated when Raffe didn’t really show up in the most part of World After because the main reason why I love this series so much is because of him <3 he is such a sweethear</span>
  <span id="freeText18235265839560344032" style="display:none">I’M REALLY SAD THAT THIS IS OVER :(((( this series was spectacular as a whole! This book was great but it did have something about it that did not quite put it up to my expectations. The character development was fantastic, the relationship growth of everyone was great and also THIS BOOK HAD THE CUTEST MOMENTS. I was really devastated when Raffe didn’t really show up in the most part of World After because the main reason why I love this series so much is because of him &lt;3 he is such a sweetheart and it doesn’t hurt that he is pretty witty ;) <br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/200_zpsjfk4tw0c.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469438901ra/19816745.gif" alt=" photo 200_zpsjfk4tw0c.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I like how Penryn grew throughout the series from someone who only thinks about protecting her family to someone who is selfless and learns to take on responsibility for a larger group of people. I also loved how she learned to accept and love her mother and sister for who they are. She has come a long way from the Penryn in Angelfall and that is great! <br>I love how they show Raffe and his friendship with the Watchers in this book but it could have been explored more! I feel like this book is short and that the ending was too abrupt to answer all the questions that I have had for this series. Still, I think that the way the characters connected in this book wasn’t really put forward well! Like, yeah I get that Raffe is attracted to Penryn but how did it change to love?? Like some of the questions that I’ve been dying to get answered didn’t get answered so I was pretty sad <br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/9478548_zps8qfsgu9a.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469438901ra/19816746.gif" alt=" photo 9478548_zps8qfsgu9a.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>However, that ONE QUOTE TOTALLY WON ME OVER LIKE AWWW <br>“I have better things to do.” <br>“Like what?” <br>He opens one eye and looks at me. “Like convince a stubborn girl to admit she’s madly in love with me.”<br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/200_s_zpsvo4s8vxi.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469438901i/19816747.gif" alt=" photo 200_s_zpsvo4s8vxi.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Overall, this book was great but I felt like there was something missing, but that doesn’t mean that this book was bad! This series was fantastic &lt;3<br></span>

<div id="review_903519919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/903519919" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/903519919?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444778557" href="/book/show/13638020-end-of-days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer903519919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3145362391669186663">It's been over a year and a half since I read the first two books so I was expecting to go into this completely blindly but this book was really helpful in reminding me of previous events! I read the entire thing and never once read a line where I had to go back and think "wait, what?" I love Raffe and Penryn's relationship. I'm a sucker for those superhuman boys matched with normal human girls, I gotta admit. It made me swoon. However, this book (as well as the earlier books...) are a bit frust</span>
  <span id="freeText3145362391669186663" style="display:none">It's been over a year and a half since I read the first two books so I was expecting to go into this completely blindly but this book was really helpful in reminding me of previous events! I read the entire thing and never once read a line where I had to go back and think "wait, what?" I love Raffe and Penryn's relationship. I'm a sucker for those superhuman boys matched with normal human girls, I gotta admit. It made me swoon. However, this book (as well as the earlier books...) are a bit frustrating because there's so much angst between them and the entire "we can't be together!!!" trope. it got kind of exhausting after a while, and even a bit useless because there were so many kissing scenes anyway. I love these books because they are just so damn fast paced, and I found myself reading and then checking the page I was on and going "WHOA seriously???" because it just flies by. These are action packed and the writing is so gripping that I read this in practically 3 sittings. My main problem with this is that it just got a little too strange for me. I like these books because there's a layer of darkness and weird sci-fi that you typically don't find in angel/post-apocalyptic books, but in this book it just got a little bit absurd and even a little hard to comprehend/visualize. Additionally, I thought that this wrapped up a little too loose-ended for my taste; I would have preferred a chapter or two at the end just to more fully explain the characters' futures. But overall a very enjoyable series and I love Penryn and Raffe and now i'm on a hunt for a man with wings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3145362391669186663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1112794404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1112794404" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1112794404?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444778557" href="/book/show/13638020-end-of-days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1112794404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer633449538372842944">So, where do I start from? Do I start from the beginning? Well, I was and still am pumped for this book, for this series. It's a great series and although Susan Ee planned for it to be a 5 book series, it ended up being just 3 books, and this is the final one. <br/><br/>I'm sad that there won't be any more books coming from this series but I'd sure as hell love to read some other book Ee releases in the future. I'm quite sure, it's going to be amazing.<br/><br/>Her short sentences, and dialogues are amazing and des</span>
  <span id="freeText633449538372842944" style="display:none">So, where do I start from? Do I start from the beginning? Well, I was and still am pumped for this book, for this series. It's a great series and although Susan Ee planned for it to be a 5 book series, it ended up being just 3 books, and this is the final one. <br /><br />I'm sad that there won't be any more books coming from this series but I'd sure as hell love to read some other book Ee releases in the future. I'm quite sure, it's going to be amazing.<br /><br />Her short sentences, and dialogues are amazing and despite my not liking dialogues all that much, she brings them on nicely and definitely adds to the amazing-ness of the story.<br /><br />So, final chapter. Is it a happily ever after or is it a disastrous ever after? You'll have to read to find out.<br /><br />If you're a fan, a shipper, of Penryn and Raffe then you'll probably love this book. It's the only book in the trilogy where we get some action between these two. Things get heated. Hot and bothered. <br /><br />The book was gripping, it didn't let me go. I couldn't even get myself to leave the book aside and go pee. Yup. That's gripping to me. Uhm, there was action, constant action, and that's what I mainly love about this series. It's a dystopia, it has angels and it involves some drool-worthy action. <br /><br />While Penryn has always been a badass, I think she's more confident in this one, she's more decisive. She becomes a leader. Raffe, okay, he's the tough type and while some authors get the whole attitude wrong, Ee did him justice, balancing the tough facade and his real self.<br /><br />I only wish that after the final battle scene, the ending of the book would have laster a little while longer so I could have said my goodbyes more properly. Oh, and yes your eyes didn't trick you, there is a battle scene and I'm telling you this because it'll make you that much more anxious throughout the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="633449538372842944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11960164402541730930" style="display:none">Buddy read with all my favorite whores: Harriet, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1172881645?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna</a>, Jenny, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277796587?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat</a>, Sarah, Portia annnnnndddddd yours trulyyyyy!!! (Click for their wonderful reviews)<br><br><br><br><b>
  <i>"It'll be tough for them to take any action while I'm pummeling their faces. Disrespect will not be tolerated."<br>I half smile at him. "Because you're all about respect."<br>He sighs as if a little disgusted with himself. "Lately, I seem to be all about you."</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/so-cute_zpszflrpynl.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422979913ra/13571413.gif" alt=" photo so-cute_zpszflrpynl.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Beautiful, mesmerizing, addicting....perfect. It's no secret to anyone that knows me that this is my second favorite series of all time-not even close. I have fangirled about this series to friends and enemies alike, if only to spread a little more of the Raffe love-oh yeah, <b>did I mention he's my number one book guy??</b> EVER? Yeah, well, most people know that as well. But what most people don't know, seeing as it's my darkest secret, is that I was so terrified I'd hate this book that I almost wasn't excited about it's upcoming release. Yeah. Shocking. But as I picked this story up and began zooming through the story, pages of the book simply evaporated into thin air as if they were never there in the first place-I was a torrential reading storm. It was as if I had never left this world...and maybe I never truly have.<br><br><br><b>Sometimes, I wish I could take a vacation from myself.</b><br><br><br>What began as a story about an archangel losing his most coveted possession, his snowy white wings, and a girl taking him 'hostage' to get her sister back became an all out war between the two races. It's almost as if Penryn was meant to run across the de-winging of my beloved Raffe all those days and nights ago. Humans are scared of angels. Angels believe man to be inferior and not worth questioning when told to slaughter them all. That is, until a certain cocky angel gets taken in by a stubborn and determined girl and they are forced to travel together for what they both want most. <b>But what happens when what they want most becomes the one thing they were taught to despise: <i>Each other</i>.</b><br><br><br><br><b>He looks down at me with sincere eyes. "If I were human, I would have been the first in line for you..." </b><br><br><br>I'd have to say that, even through all the searching and war and battles, this has to be my favorite forbidden love story. And no, there's so much more to this series than an angel bereft of his wings who has 'secretly' fallen for a daughter of man. I realize this. I've processed that. And my conclusion is this: While the <b>story is amazing, unforgettable, and utterly epic</b>, it wouldn't mean half of what it did to me without Penryn and Raffe's unattainable love for one another. They are by far the cutest, sweetest, <i>fiercest</i> enemies I've ever stumbled across, and <b>I highly doubt I'll cross paths with a couple that will ever mean more to me than them</b>....and that's a bold statement on my part: <b>I'm the whore of ships.</b> <br><br><br><b>He's still scrutinizing my outfit. "Are you wearing men's shorts?"<br>"I guess so. But they fit."<br>"Whose are they?"<br>"Nobody's. I found them in a drawer."<br>He reaches over and pulls a thread off the frayed leg. It unravels, slowly winding it's way around my thigh and incrementally shortening the already short shorts.<br>"What would you do if you had to make a run for it?" His voice is husky as he stares, mesmerized, at the unraveling thread.<br>"I'd grab my shoes and run."<br>"Dressed like this? In front of lawless men?" His eyes drift up to my midriff.</b><br><br><br>Every character was beyond wonderful in this story (main characters, let's not be hasty). We got more Paige, some of Penryn's crazy mom (Whom I absolutely adored in this installment), and some wonderful new Watchers. Each character added an intricate layer to the story that made it impossible not to fall harder and, in the end, they even added to Raffryn's (YES, I WENT THERE-WHAT OF IT?) relationship. An amazing love scene is one thing, but added laughter, friendship, awkward instances, family love moments...that all makes it even better. One minute I'm swooning, then two seconds later I'm giggling and squeeing all at once (Keaton avoided me at all costs during this voyage through my beloved Raffe land-I was not to be trifled with as I fangirled openly) and unable to control the RIDICULOUS smile on my face. <br><br><br><b>The sun is beginning to set, adding a golden glow to the water. Wisps of mist begin creeping over the bay. It should be a peaceful scene, only my blood feels like it's freezing by the second.</b><br><br><br>I can't sign off of this series without saying something that is very important: Susan Ee is the Queen. Elaborate? Of course, my mistake. <b>She's the Queen of: Writing, characterization, gore, disturbing images, forbidden love, epic battle scenes, epic tormented love....</b> Need I <i>really</i> go on? This woman is my hero, from her creepy locust thingies that tore my heart out in book one to the creepy monster we see in the finale, no one has ever made me love evil (and now sometimes lovable, thanks to a certain sister) beings more than this author. She made me smile maliciously so many times I swear you could have caught me twirling my metaphorical mustache more than once in each installment. <b>Breathless, heart-pounding, soul-crushing moments</b> are her specialty, and I am in first in line when she serves them up...and no one is likely to take that accomplishment from her in my mind anytime soon (Kagawa is the only one likely on the same playing field, but I refuse to give either of them a step above the other-they're both wonderful, sick, evil beings).<br><br><br>Anyone over my fangirling yet? <b>Too bad.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/Phoebe-Gifs-friends-16836441-500-200_zps8ebl7pjb.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423592627ra/13648163.gif" alt=" photo Phoebe-Gifs-friends-16836441-500-200_zps8ebl7pjb.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>You don't have to keep reading lol, but this is my final Raffe review and I will not stop before it's all out. <br><br><br><br><b>Without his feathered wings, the angels won't accept him. And regardless of what kind of wings he has, humans won't accept him either. <br>Uriel or someone in his crew once said that angels were made to be part of a pack, but no matter where Raffe goes, he always seems to be the outsider.</b><br><br><br>The way Raffe protects, takes care of, treats, saves, lives for Penryn shattered my heart into a million tiny pieces. The love he tries to hide so he can save his brethren throughout the series crushed my soul (in the <b>best</b> possible way). And the way he longs for Pen.....it made me so beyond happy I could barely breathe. Nothing compares to his jealousies, his devastation that he can't be with her because it could never be in the world they live in. This installment <b>capitalized on all those wonderful feelings we got from book one and multiplied them into this tragic and epic betrayal of what they both want more than their next breath</b>-I teared up so many times it bordered on crazy. Even after they repeatedly say goodbye, is there a way to make it work?<br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_n87phrQr181t0z40ro1_500_zps94v9e1sd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431528212i/14843536.jpg" alt=" photo tumblr_n87phrQr181t0z40ro1_500_zps94v9e1sd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I could not have loved this more. I don't care about literally any of the flaws, any world-building faux pas my lovely and aggravating friends found to be incriminating, or any of the beyond disturbing and nightmare inducing images. Any flaw is minuscule to the immense enjoyment I found while reading this wonderful, addicting, and, again, <b>UNFORGETTABLE</b> series about a beautiful, tormented, and lonely angel who feels the only person he can trust in the world is the daughter of man who once took him hostage. Nothing compares to the feelings I got while reading this and I will perpetually re-read this series until I know it word for word and scene by scene. I would say, 'Hey, you HAVE to read this,' but everyone and their brother has read it. Dude, my GRANDMOTHER has read this and began this final installment yesterday, like me. What kind of person hasn't? Do you live under a rock?? Bro, step it up! And seriously, Raffe, enough about the farming lol. That won't win Penryn-we don't live in 1950 (or whenever-psh).<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>*************************<br>I BEGIN NOW!!!!!!<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/b7a5b5d9a27386d1f9024c71f92584b4_zpstvkordqf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431434589i/14837201.jpg" alt=" photo b7a5b5d9a27386d1f9024c71f92584b4_zpstvkordqf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>********************************************************<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><b>OMG SO PRETTEH!!!!!! AGHHHHHH!!!!! <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/13638020_zpst0y8a4ic.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423248155i/13600522.jpg" alt=" photo 13638020_zpst0y8a4ic.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br><br>RAFFEEEEEEEEE!!!!!! I NEED YOU, LIKE, YESTERDAY ♥</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11960164402541730930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

How far we've come! Excited to see how Penryn's story ends. (And very glad we don't have to wait for another 3 books to find out!)</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rtZ/NivgFbbukiB2jOfWGChwGcnRmATDCD9ZZ6ti+i4iv/owoh3TeR17mDL4HW1alQRyeP/hZkctx5y5lOhZwA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fMkJ0yDws66VqSds05PYW8CDfMhlB3hYKOFo/7xj76PwoIzVqQ11YWZAnyinaWMZffcXeUt+GtwNGa0hg+lMTQ==')})
  }
